47: 
48: ## Command Instructions
49: 
50: <skill-instruction>
51: Base directory for this skill: E:\opencode-config\skills\brainstorming/
52: File references ([file not found: E:\opencode-config\skills\brainstorming\path)] in this skill are relative to this directory.
53: 
54: # Brainstorming Ideas Into Designs
55: 
56: Help turn ideas into fully formed designs and specs through natural collaborative dialogue.
57: 
58: Start by understanding the current project context, then ask questions one at a time to refine the idea. Once you understand what you're building, present the design and get user approval.
59: 
60: <HARD-GATE>
61: Do NOT invoke any implementation skill, write any code, scaffold any project, or take any implementation action until you have presented a design and the user has approved it. This applies to EVERY project regardless of perceived simplicity.
62: </HARD-GATE>
63: 
64: ## Anti-Pattern: "This Is Too Simple To Need A Design"
65: 
66: Every project goes through this process. A todo list, a single-function utility, a config change — all of them. "Simple" projects are where unexamined assumptions cause the most wasted work. The design can be short (a few sentences for truly simple projects), but you MUST present it and get approval.
67: 
68: ## Checklist
69: 
70: You MUST create a task for each of these items and complete them in order:
71: 
72: 1. **Explore project context** — check files, docs, recent commits
73: 2. **Offer visual companion** (if topic will involve visual questions) — this is its own message, not combined with a clarifying question. See the Visual Companion section below.
74: 3. **Ask clarifying questions** — one at a time, understand purpose/constraints/success criteria
75: 4. **Propose 2-3 approaches** — with trade-offs and your recommendation
76: 5. **Present design** — in sections scaled to their complexity, get user approval after each section
77: 6. **Write design doc** — save to `docs/superpowers/specs/YYYY-MM-DD-<topic>-design.md` and commit
78: 7. **Spec self-review** — quick inline check for placeholders, contradictions, ambiguity, scope (see below)
79: 8. **User reviews written spec** — ask user to review the spec file before proceeding
80: 9. **Transition to implementation** — invoke writing-plans skill to create implementation plan
81: 
82: ## Process Flow
83: 
84: ```dot
85: digraph brainstorming {
86:     "Explore project context" [shape=box];
87:     "Visual questions ahead?" [shape=diamond];
88:     "Offer Visual Companion\n(own message, no other content)" [shape=box];
89:     "Ask clarifying questions" [shape=box];
90:     "Propose 2-3 approaches" [shape=box];
91:     "Present design sections" [shape=box];
92:     "User approves design?" [shape=diamond];
93:     "Write design doc" [shape=box];
94:     "Spec self-review\n(fix inline)" [shape=box];
95:     "User reviews spec?" [shape=diamond];
96:     "Invoke writing-plans skill" [shape=doublecircle];
97: 
98:     "Explore project context" -> "Visual questions ahead?";
99:     "Visual questions ahead?" -> "Offer Visual Companion\n(own message, no other content)" [label="yes"];
100:     "Visual questions ahead?" -> "Ask clarifying questions" [label="no"];
101:     "Offer Visual Companion\n(own message, no other content)" -> "Ask clarifying questions";
102:     "Ask clarifying questions" -> "Propose 2-3 approaches";
103:     "Propose 2-3 approaches" -> "Present design sections";
104:     "Present design sections" -> "User approves design?";
105:     "User approves design?" -> "Present design sections" [label="no, revise"];
106:     "User approves design?" -> "Write design doc" [label="yes"];
107:     "Write design doc" -> "Spec self-review\n(fix inline)";
108:     "Spec self-review\n(fix inline)" -> "User reviews spec?";
109:     "User reviews spec?" -> "Write design doc" [label="changes requested"];
110:     "User reviews spec?" -> "Invoke writing-plans skill" [label="approved"];
111: }
112: ```
113: 
114: **The terminal state is invoking writing-plans.** Do NOT invoke frontend-design, mcp-builder, or any other implementation skill. The ONLY skill you invoke after brainstorming is writing-plans.
115: 
116: ## The Process
117: 
118: **Understanding the idea:**
119: 
120: - Check out the current project state first (files, docs, recent commits)
121: - Before asking detailed questions, assess scope: if the request describes multiple independent subsystems (e.g., "build a platform with chat, file storage, billing, and analytics"), flag this immediately. Don't spend questions refining details of a project that needs to be decomposed first.
122: - If the project is too large for a single spec, help the user decompose into sub-projects: what are the independent pieces, how do they relate, what order should they be built? Then brainstorm the first sub-project through the normal design flow. Each sub-project gets its own spec → plan → implementation cycle.
123: - For appropriately-scoped projects, ask questions one at a time to refine the idea
124: - Prefer multiple choice questions when possible, but open-ended is fine too
125: - Only one question per message - if a topic needs more exploration, break it into multiple questions
126: - Focus on understanding: purpose, constraints, success criteria
127: 
128: **Exploring approaches:**
129: 
130: - Propose 2-3 different approaches with trade-offs
131: - Present options conversationally with your recommendation and reasoning
132: - Lead with your recommended option and explain why
133: 
134: **Presenting the design:**
135: 
136: - Once you believe you understand what you're building, present the design
137: - Scale each section to its complexity: a few sentences if straightforward, up to 200-300 words if nuanced
138: - Ask after each section whether it looks right so far
139: - Cover: architecture, components, data flow, error handling, testing
140: - Be ready to go back and clarify if something doesn't make sense
141: 
142: **Design for isolation and clarity:**
143: 
144: - Break the system into smaller units that each have one clear purpose, communicate through well-defined interfaces, and can be understood and tested independently
145: - For each unit, you should be able to answer: what does it do, how do you use it, and what does it depend on?
146: - Can someone understand what a unit does without reading its internals? Can you change the internals without breaking consumers? If not, the boundaries need work.
147: - Smaller, well-bounded units are also easier for you to work with - you reason better about code you can hold in context at once, and your edits are more reliable when files are focused. When a file grows large, that's often a signal that it's doing too much.
148: 
149: **Working in existing codebases:**
150: 
151: - Explore the current structure before proposing changes. Follow existing patterns.
152: - Where existing code has problems that affect the work (e.g., a file that's grown too large, unclear boundaries, tangled responsibilities), include targeted improvements as part of the design - the way a good developer improves code they're working in.
153: - Don't propose unrelated refactoring. Stay focused on what serves the current goal.
154: 
155: ## After the Design
156: 
157: **Documentation:**
158: 
159: - Write the validated design (spec) to `docs/superpowers/specs/YYYY-MM-DD-<topic>-design.md`
160:   - (User preferences for spec location override this default)
161: - Use elements-of-style:writing-clearly-and-concisely skill if available
162: - Commit the design document to git
163: 
164: **Spec Self-Review:**
165: After writing the spec document, look at it with fresh eyes:
166: 
167: 1. **Placeholder scan:** Any "TBD", "TODO", incomplete sections, or vague requirements? Fix them.
168: 2. **Internal consistency:** Do any sections contradict each other? Does the architecture match the feature descriptions?
169: 3. **Scope check:** Is this focused enough for a single implementation plan, or does it need decomposition?
170: 4. **Ambiguity check:** Could any requirement be interpreted two different ways? If so, pick one and make it explicit.
171: 
172: Fix any issues inline. No need to re-review — just fix and move on.
173: 
174: **User Review Gate:**
175: After the spec review loop passes, ask the user to review the written spec before proceeding:
176: 
177: > "Spec written and committed to `<path>`. Please review it and let me know if you want to make any changes before we start writing out the implementation plan."
178: 
179: Wait for the user's response. If they request changes, make them and re-run the spec review loop. Only proceed once the user approves.
180: 
181: **Implementation:**
182: 
183: - Invoke the writing-plans skill to create a detailed implementation plan
184: - Do NOT invoke any other skill. writing-plans is the next step.
185: 
186: ## Key Principles
187: 
188: - **One question at a time** - Don't overwhelm with multiple questions
189: - **Multiple choice preferred** - Easier to answer than open-ended when possible
190: - **YAGNI ruthlessly** - Remove unnecessary features from all designs
191: - **Explore alternatives** - Always propose 2-3 approaches before settling
192: - **Incremental validation** - Present design, get approval before moving on
193: - **Be flexible** - Go back and clarify when something doesn't make sense
194: 
195: ## Visual Companion
196: 
197: A browser-based companion for showing mockups, diagrams, and visual options during brainstorming. Available as a tool — not a mode. Accepting the companion means it's available for questions that benefit from visual treatment; it does NOT mean every question goes through the browser.
198: 
199: **Offering the companion:** When you anticipate that upcoming questions will involve visual content (mockups, layouts, diagrams), offer it once for consent:
200: > "Some of what we're working on might be easier to explain if I can show it to you in a web browser. I can put together mockups, diagrams, comparisons, and other visuals as we go. This feature is still new and can be token-intensive. Want to try it? (Requires opening a local URL)"
201: 
202: **This offer MUST be its own message.** Do not combine it with clarifying questions, context summaries, or any other content. The message should contain ONLY the offer above and nothing else. Wait for the user's response before continuing. If they decline, proceed with text-only brainstorming.
203: 
204: **Per-question decision:** Even after the user accepts, decide FOR EACH QUESTION whether to use the browser or the terminal. The test: **would the user understand this better by seeing it than reading it?**
205: 
206: - **Use the browser** for content that IS visual — mockups, wireframes, layout comparisons, architecture diagrams, side-by-side visual designs
207: - **Use the terminal** for content that is text — requirements questions, conceptual choices, tradeoff lists, A/B/C/D text options, scope decisions
208: 
209: A question about a UI topic is not automatically a visual question. "What does personality mean in this context?" is a conceptual question — use the terminal. "Which wizard layout works better?" is a visual question — use the browser.
210: 
211: If they agree to the companion, read the detailed guide before proceeding:
212: `skills/brainstorming/visual-companion.md`
213: </skill-instruction>

1772: 37: <auto-slash-command>
1773: 38: # /brainstorming Command
1774: 39: 
1775: 40: **Description**: (opencode - Skill) You MUST use this before any creative work - creating features, building components, adding functionality, or modifying behavior. Explores user intent, requirements and design before implementation.
1776: 41:

1778: 43: 
1779: 44: **Scope**: skill
1780: 45: 
1781: 46: ---
1782: 47: 
1783: 48: ## Command Instructions
1784: 49: 
1785: 50: <skill-instruction>
1786: 51: Base directory for this skill: E:\opencode-config\skills\brainstorming/
1787: 52: File references ([file not found: E:\opencode-config\skills\brainstorming\path)] in this skill are relative to this directory.
1788: 53: 
1789: 54: # Brainstorming Ideas Into Designs
1790: 55: 
1791: 56: Help turn ideas into fully formed designs and specs through natural collaborative dialogue.
1792: 57: 
1793: 58: Start by understanding the current project context, then ask questions one at a time to refine the idea. Once you understand what you're building, present the design and get user approval.
1794: 59: 
1795: 60: <HARD-GATE>
1796: 61: Do NOT invoke any implementation skill, write any code, scaffold any project, or take any implementation action until you have presented a design and the user has approved it. This applies to EVERY project regardless of perceived simplicity.
1797: 62: </HARD-GATE>
1798: 63: 
1799: 64: ## Anti-Pattern: "This Is Too Simple To Need A Design"
1800: 65: 
1801: 66: Every project goes through this process. A todo list, a single-function utility, a config change — all of them. "Simple" projects are where unexamined assumptions cause the most wasted work. The design can be short (a few sentences for truly simple projects), but you MUST present it and get approval.
1802: 67: 
1803: 68: ## Checklist
1804: 69: 
1805: 70: You MUST create a task for each of these items and complete them in order:
1806: 71: 
1807: 72: 1. **Explore project context** — check files, docs, recent commits
1808: 73: 2. **Offer visual companion** (if topic will involve visual questions) — this is its own message, not combined with a clarifying question. See the Visual Companion section below.
1809: 74: 3. **Ask clarifying questions** — one at a time, understand purpose/constraints/success criteria
1810: 75: 4. **Propose 2-3 approaches** — with trade-offs and your recommendation
1811: 76: 5. **Present design** — in sections scaled to their complexity, get user approval after each section
1812: 77: 6. **Write design doc** — save to `docs/superpowers/specs/YYYY-MM-DD-<topic>-design.md` and commit
1813: 78: 7. **Spec self-review** — quick inline check for placeholders, contradictions, ambiguity, scope (see below)
1814: 79: 8. **User reviews written spec** — ask user to review the spec file before proceeding
1815: 80: 9. **Transition to implementation** — invoke writing-plans skill to create implementation plan
1816: 81: 
1817: 82: ## Process Flow
1818: 83: 
1819: 84: ```dot
1820: 85: digraph brainstorming {
1821: 86:     "Explore project context" [shape=box];
1822: 87:     "Visual questions ahead?" [shape=diamond];
1823: 88:     "Offer Visual Companion\n(own message, no other content)" [shape=box];
1824: 89:     "Ask clarifying questions" [shape=box];
1825: 90:     "Propose 2-3 approaches" [shape=box];
1826: 91:     "Present design sections" [shape=box];
1827: 92:     "User approves design?" [shape=diamond];
1828: 93:     "Write design doc" [shape=box];
1829: 94:     "Spec self-review\n(fix inline)" [shape=box];
1830: 95:     "User reviews spec?" [shape=diamond];
1831: 96:     "Invoke writing-plans skill" [shape=doublecircle];
1832: 97: 
1833: 98:     "Explore project context" -> "Visual questions ahead?";
1834: 99:     "Visual questions ahead?" -> "Offer Visual Companion\n(own message, no other content)" [label="yes"];
1835: 100:     "Visual questions ahead?" -> "Ask clarifying questions" [label="no"];
1836: 101:     "Offer Visual Companion\n(own message, no other content)" -> "Ask clarifying questions";
1837: 102:     "Ask clarifying questions" -> "Propose 2-3 approaches";
1838: 103:     "Propose 2-3 approaches" -> "Present design sections";
1839: 104:     "Present design sections" -> "User approves design?";
1840: 105:     "User approves design?" -> "Present design sections" [label="no, revise"];
1841: 106:     "User approves design?" -> "Write design doc" [label="yes"];
1842: 107:     "Write design doc" -> "Spec self-review\n(fix inline)";
1843: 108:     "Spec self-review\n(fix inline)" -> "User reviews spec?";
1844: 109:     "User reviews spec?" -> "Write design doc" [label="changes requested"];
1845: 110:     "User reviews spec?" -> "Invoke writing-plans skill" [label="approved"];
1846: 111: }
1847: 112: ```
1848: 113: 
1849: 114: **The terminal state is invoking writing-plans.** Do NOT invoke frontend-design, mcp-builder, or any other implementation skill. The ONLY skill you invoke after brainstorming is writing-plans.
1850: 115: 
1851: 116: ## The Process
1852: 117: 
1853: 118: **Understanding the idea:**
1854: 119: 
1855: 120: - Check out the current project state first (files, docs, recent commits)
1856: 121: - Before asking detailed questions, assess scope: if the request describes multiple independent subsystems (e.g., "build a platform with chat, file storage, billing, and analytics"), flag this immediately. Don't spend questions refining details of a project that needs to be decomposed first.
1857: 122: - If the project is too large for a single spec, help the user decompose into sub-projects: what are the independent pieces, how do they relate, what order should they be built? Then brainstorm the first sub-project through the normal design flow. Each sub-project gets its own spec → plan → implementation cycle.
1858: 123: - For appropriately-scoped projects, ask questions one at a time to refine the idea
1859: 124: - Prefer multiple choice questions when possible, but open-ended is fine too
1860: 125: - Only one question per message - if a topic needs more exploration, break it into multiple questions
1861: 126: - Focus on understanding: purpose, constraints, success criteria
1862: 127: 
1863: 128: **Exploring approaches:**
1864: 129: 
1865: 130: - Propose 2-3 different approaches with trade-offs
1866: 131: - Present options conversationally with your recommendation and reasoning
1867: 132: - Lead with your recommended option and explain why
1868: 133: 
1869: 134: **Presenting the design:**
1870: 135: 
1871: 136: - Once you believe you understand what you're building, present the design
1872: 137: - Scale each section to its complexity: a few sentences if straightforward, up to 200-300 words if nuanced
1873: 138: - Ask after each section whether it looks right so far
1874: 139: - Cover: architecture, components, data flow, error handling, testing
1875: 140: - Be ready to go back and clarify if something doesn't make sense
1876: 141: 
1877: 142: **Design for isolation and clarity:**
1878: 143: 
1879: 144: - Break the system into smaller units that each have one clear purpose, communicate through well-defined interfaces, and can be understood and tested independently
1880: 145: - For each unit, you should be able to answer: what does it do, how do you use it, and what does it depend on?
1881: 146: - Can someone understand what a unit does without reading its internals? Can you change the internals without breaking consumers? If not, the boundaries need work.
1882: 147: - Smaller, well-bounded units are also easier for you to work with - you reason better about code you can hold in context at once, and your edits are more reliable when files are focused. When a file grows large, that's often a signal that it's doing too much.
1883: 148: 
1884: 149: **Working in existing codebases:**
1885: 150: 
1886: 151: - Explore the current structure before proposing changes. Follow existing patterns.
1887: 152: - Where existing code has problems that affect the work (e.g., a file that's grown too large, unclear boundaries, tangled responsibilities), include targeted improvements as part of the design - the way a good developer improves code they're working in.
1888: 153: - Don't propose unrelated refactoring. Stay focused on what serves the current goal.
1889: 154: 
1890: 155: ## After the Design
1891: 156: 
1892: 157: **Documentation:**
1893: 158: 
1894: 159: - Write the validated design (spec) to `docs/superpowers/specs/YYYY-MM-DD-<topic>-design.md`
1895: 160:   - (User preferences for spec location override this default)
1896: 161: - Use elements-of-style:writing-clearly-and-concisely skill if available
1897: 162: - Commit the design document to git
1898: 163: 
1899: 164: **Spec Self-Review:**
1900: 165: After writing the spec document, look at it with fresh eyes:
1901: 166: 
1902: 167: 1. **Placeholder scan:** Any "TBD", "TODO", incomplete sections, or vague requirements? Fix them.
1903: 168: 2. **Internal consistency:** Do any sections contradict each other? Does the architecture match the feature descriptions?
1904: 169: 3. **Scope check:** Is this focused enough for a single implementation plan, or does it need decomposition?
1905: 170: 4. **Ambiguity check:** Could any requirement be interpreted two different ways? If so, pick one and make it explicit.
1906: 171: 
1907: 172: Fix any issues inline. No need to re-review — just fix and move on.
1908: 173: 
1909: 174: **User Review Gate:**
1910: 175: After the spec review loop passes, ask the user to review the written spec before proceeding:
1911: 176: 
1912: 177: > "Spec written and committed to `<path>`. Please review it and let me know if you want to make any changes before we start writing out the implementation plan."
1913: 178: 
1914: 179: Wait for the user's response. If they request changes, make them and re-run the spec review loop. Only proceed once the user approves.
1915: 180: 
1916: 181: **Implementation:**
1917: 182: 
1918: 183: - Invoke the writing-plans skill to create a detailed implementation plan
1919: 184: - Do NOT invoke any other skill. writing-plans is the next step.
1920: 185: 
1921: 186: ## Key Principles
1922: 187: 
1923: 188: - **One question at a time** - Don't overwhelm with multiple questions
1924: 189: - **Multiple choice preferred** - Easier to answer than open-ended when possible
1925: 190: - **YAGNI ruthlessly** - Remove unnecessary features from all designs
1926: 191: - **Explore alternatives** - Always propose 2-3 approaches before settling
1927: 192: - **Incremental validation** - Present design, get approval before moving on
1928: 193: - **Be flexible** - Go back and clarify when something doesn't make sense
1929: 194: 
1930: 195: ## Visual Companion
1931: 196: 
1932: 197: A browser-based companion for showing mockups, diagrams, and visual options during brainstorming. Available as a tool — not a mode. Accepting the companion means it's available for questions that benefit from visual treatment; it does NOT mean every question goes through the browser.
1933: 198: 
1934: 199: **Offering the companion:** When you anticipate that upcoming questions will involve visual content (mockups, layouts, diagrams), offer it once for consent:
1935: 200: > "Some of what we're working on might be easier to explain if I can show it to you in a web browser. I can put together mockups, diagrams, comparisons, and other visuals as we go. This feature is still new and can be token-intensive. Want to try it? (Requires opening a local URL)"
1936: 201: 
1937: 202: **This offer MUST be its own message.** Do not combine it with clarifying questions, context summaries, or any other content. The message should contain ONLY the offer above and nothing else. Wait for the user's response before continuing. If they decline, proceed with text-only brainstorming.
1938: 203: 
1939: 204: **Per-question decision:** Even after the user accepts, decide FOR EACH QUESTION whether to use the browser or the terminal. The test: **would the user understand this better by seeing it than reading it?**
1940: 205: 
1941: 206: - **Use the browser** for content that IS visual — mockups, wireframes, layout comparisons, architecture diagrams, side-by-side visual designs
1942: 207: - **Use the terminal** for content that is text — requirements questions, conceptual choices, tradeoff lists, A/B/C/D text options, scope decisions
1943: 208: 
1944: 209: A question about a UI topic is not automatically a visual question. "What does personality mean in this context?" is a conceptual question — use the terminal. "Which wizard layout works better?" is a visual question — use the browser.
1945: 210: 
1946: 211: If they agree to the companion, read the detailed guide before proceeding:
1947: 212: `skills/brainstorming/visual-companion.md`
1948: 213: </skill-instruction>
1949: 214: 
1950: 215: <user-request>
1951: 216: 目前这个项目是我通过CVAT得到的原图和AOI划分图，你先分析一下目前的目录结构，在帮我选取合适的模型，我想着在现有的模型上通过我的提前标注来微调模型，从而做语义分割。图片大概有120张，目前是40张，我先做一些实验。
1952: 217: </user-request>

2020: 285:     "Spec self-review\n(fix inline)" -> "User reviews spec?";
2021: 286:     "User reviews spec?" -> "Write design doc" [label="changes requested"];
2022: 287:     "User reviews spec?" -> "Invoke writing-plans skill" [label="approved"];
2023: 288: }
2024: 289: ```
2025: 290: 
2026: 291: **The terminal state is invoking writing-plans.** Do NOT invoke frontend-design, mcp-builder, or any other implementation skill. The ONLY skill you invoke after brainstorming is writing-plans.
2027: 292: 
2028: 293: ## The Process
2029: 294: 
2030: 295: **Understanding the idea:**
2031: 296: 
2032: 297: - Check out the current project state first (files, docs, recent commits)
2033: 298: - Before asking detailed questions, assess scope: if the request describes multiple independent subsystems (e.g., "build a platform with chat, file storage, billing, and analytics"), flag this immediately. Don't spend questions refining details of a project that needs to be decomposed first.
2034: 299: - If the project is too large for a single spec, help the user decompose into sub-projects: what are the independent pieces, how do they relate, what order should they be built? Then brainstorm the first sub-project through the normal design flow. Each sub-project gets its own spec → plan → implementation cycle.
2035: 300: - For appropriately-scoped projects, ask questions one at a time to refine the idea
2036: 301: - Prefer multiple choice questions when possible, but open-ended is fine too
2037: 302: - Only one question per message - if a topic needs more exploration, break it into multiple questions
2038: 303: - Focus on understanding: purpose, constraints, success criteria
2039: 304: 
2040: 305: **Exploring approaches:**
2041: 306: 
2042: 307: - Propose 2-3 different approaches with trade-offs
2043: 308: - Present options conversationally with your recommendation and reasoning
2044: 309: - Lead with your recommended option and explain why
2045: 310: 
2046: 311: **Presenting the design:**
2047: 312: 
2048: 313: - Once you believe you understand what you're building, present the design
2049: 314: - Scale each section to its complexity: a few sentences if straightforward, up to 200-300 words if nuanced
2050: 315: - Ask after each section whether it looks right so far
2051: 316: - Cover: architecture, components, data flow, error handling, testing
2052: 317: - Be ready to go back and clarify if something doesn't make sense
2053: 318: 
2054: 319: **Design for isolation and clarity:**
2055: 320: 
2056: 321: - Break the system into smaller units that each have one clear purpose, communicate through well-defined interfaces, and can be understood and tested independently
2057: 322: - For each unit, you should be able to answer: what does it do, how do you use it, and what does it depend on?
2058: 323: - Can someone understand what a unit does without reading its internals? Can you change the internals without breaking consumers? If not, the boundaries need work.
2059: 324: - Smaller, well-bounded units are also easier for you to work with - you reason better about code you can hold in context at once, and your edits are more reliable when files are focused. When a file grows large, that's often a signal that it's doing too much.
2060: 325: 
2061: 326: **Working in existing codebases:**
2062: 327: 
2063: 328: - Explore the current structure before proposing changes. Follow existing patterns.
2064: 329: - Where existing code has problems that affect the work (e.g., a file that's grown too large, unclear boundaries, tangled responsibilities), include targeted improvements as part of the design - the way a good developer improves code they're working in.
2065: 330: - Don't propose unrelated refactoring. Stay focused on what serves the current goal.
2066: 331: 
2067: 332: ## After the Design
2068: 333: 
2069: 334: **Documentation:**
2070: 335: 
2071: 336: - Write the validated design (spec) to `docs/superpowers/specs/YYYY-MM-DD-<topic>-design.md`
2072: 337:   - (User preferences for spec location override this default)
2073: 338: - Use elements-of-style:writing-clearly-and-concisely skill if available
2074: 339: - Commit the design document to git
2075: 340: 
2076: 341: **Spec Self-Review:**
2077: 342: After writing the spec document, look at it with fresh eyes:
2078: 343: 
2079: 344: 1. **Placeholder scan:** Any "TBD", "TODO", incomplete sections, or vague requirements? Fix them.
2080: 345: 2. **Internal consistency:** Do any sections contradict each other? Does the architecture match the feature descriptions?
2081: 346: 3. **Scope check:** Is this focused enough for a single implementation plan, or does it need decomposition?
2082: 347: 4. **Ambiguity check:** Could any requirement be interpreted two different ways? If so, pick one and make it explicit.
2083: 348: 
2084: 349: Fix any issues inline. No need to re-review — just fix and move on.
2085: 350: 
2086: 351: **User Review Gate:**
2087: 352: After the spec review loop passes, ask the user to review the written spec before proceeding:
2088: 353: 
2089: 354: > "Spec written and committed to `<path>`. Please review it and let me know if you want to make any changes before we start writing out the implementation plan."
2090: 355: 
2091: 356: Wait for the user's response. If they request changes, make them and re-run the spec review loop. Only proceed once the user approves.
2092: 357: 
2093: 358: **Implementation:**
2094: 359: 
2095: 360: - Invoke the writing-plans skill to create a detailed implementation plan
2096: 361: - Do NOT invoke any other skill. writing-plans is the next step.
2097: 362: 
2098: 363: ## Key Principles
2099: 364: 
2100: 365: - **One question at a time** - Don't overwhelm with multiple questions
2101: 366: - **Multiple choice preferred** - Easier to answer than open-ended when possible
2102: 367: - **YAGNI ruthlessly** - Remove unnecessary features from all designs
2103: 368: - **Explore alternatives** - Always propose 2-3 approaches before settling
2104: 369: - **Incremental validation** - Present design, get approval before moving on
2105: 370: - **Be flexible** - Go back and clarify when something doesn't make sense
2106: 371: 
2107: 372: ## Visual Companion
2108: 373: 
2109: 374: A browser-based companion for showing mockups, diagrams, and visual options during brainstorming. Available as a tool — not a mode. Accepting the companion means it's available for questions that benefit from visual treatment; it does NOT mean every question goes through the browser.
2110: 375: 
2111: 376: **Offering the companion:** When you anticipate that upcoming questions will involve visual content (mockups, layouts, diagrams), offer it once for consent:
2112: 377: > "Some of what we're working on might be easier to explain if I can show it to you in a web browser. I can put together mockups, diagrams, comparisons, and other visuals as we go. This feature is still new and can be token-intensive. Want to try it? (Requires opening a local URL)"
2113: 378: 
2114: 379: **This offer MUST be its own message.** Do not combine it with clarifying questions, context summaries, or any other content. The message should contain ONLY the offer above and nothing else. Wait for the user's response before continuing. If they decline, proceed with text-only brainstorming.
2115: 380: 
2116: 381: **Per-question decision:** Even after the user accepts, decide FOR EACH QUESTION whether to use the browser or the terminal. The test: **would the user understand this better by seeing it than reading it?**
2117: 382: 
2118: 383: - **Use the browser** for content that IS visual — mockups, wireframes, layout comparisons, architecture diagrams, side-by-side visual designs
2119: 384: - **Use the terminal** for content that is text — requirements questions, conceptual choices, tradeoff lists, A/B/C/D text options, scope decisions
2120: 385: 
2121: 386: A question about a UI topic is not automatically a visual question. "What does personality mean in this context?" is a conceptual question — use the terminal. "Which wizard layout works better?" is a visual question — use the browser.
2122: 387: 
2123: 388: If they agree to the companion, read the detailed guide before proceeding:
2124: 389: `skills/brainstorming/visual-companion.md`
2125: 390: </skill-instruction>
2126: 391: 
2127: 392: <user-request>

3770: ### 6. Critical Preprocessing Requirement
3771: 
3772: The SegmentationClass masks are **RGB color-coded**, NOT single-channel class index maps. For training any semantic segmentation model (which expects integer class IDs 0–C), you MUST convert the RGB values to class indices. The RGB-to-class-ID mapping is:
3773: 
3774: ```python
3775: color_to_class = {
3776:     (0,0,0): 0,        # background
3777:     (12,54,138): 1,    # crowd
3778:     (131,214,41): 2,   # public facilities
3779:     (180,40,5): 3,     # commercial
3780:     (103,22,84): 4,    # ground paving
3781:     (97,196,248): 5,   # sky
3782:     (233,161,3): 6,    # building interface
3783:     (60,5,5): 7,       # cultural decoration
3784:     (12,170,34): 8,    # green landscape
3785:     (78,78,78): 9,     # vehicles
3786: }
3787: ```
3788: 
3789: ### 7. Image Naming Alignment
3790: 
3791: All 39 images in `南原图` have matching masks in both `SegmentationClass/` and `SegmentationObject/`. The naming convention is consistent: `南IMG_XXXX` (stem) + `.JPG` for images, `.png` for masks.

3858: 
3859: # Semantic Segmentation Model Comparison for Small-Dataset Fine-Tuning
3860: 
3861: > **Use case**: 40–120 annotated images from CVAT, custom AOI classes, experimental phase  
3862: > **Date**: May 2026
3863: 
3864: ---
3865: 
3866: ## Executive Summary
3867: 
3868: For **40–120 images** with custom AOI segmentation masks, the practical choice is between three approaches:
3869: 
3870: | Rank | Model | Key Strength | Why for Your Use Case |
3871: |------|-------|-------------|----------------------|
3872: | **🥇 1st** | **SegFormer-B0/B1** | Best accuracy-to-parameter ratio; HuggingFace-native | 3.8M params fits any GPU; official HF fine-tuning tutorial exists |
3873: | **🥈 2nd** | **DeepLabV3+ (MobileNet-V3-Large)** | Fastest iteration cycle; torchvision built-in | 11M params; zero extra dependencies |
3874: | **🥉 3rd** | **U-Net (EfficientNet-b0/b1 backbone)** | Best for extreme small data; augmentation-friendly | SMP library makes it trivial; proven in medical (50–500 image) settings |
3875: 
3876: **SAM and Mask2Former are not recommended** for this phase — they overfit on 40–120 images and require orders of magnitude more data to justify their complexity.
3877: 
3878: ---
3879: 
3880: ## 1. Model-by-Model Deep Dive
3881: 
3882: ### 1.1 SegFormer (Transformer-based)
3883: 
3884: | Property | Value |
3885: |----------|-------|
3886: | **Paper** | SegFormer: Simple and Efficient Design for Semantic Segmentation with Transformers (Xie et al., NeurIPS 2021) |
3887: | **Variants** | B0 (3.8M), B1 (13.7M), B2 (24.7M), B3 (44.6M), B4 (61.4M), B5 (84.7M) |
3888: | **Architecture** | Hierarchical Transformer encoder (MiT) + lightweight all-MLP decoder head |
3889: | **Key innovation** | No positional encoding needed → robust to resolution changes; hierarchical features from Transformer |
3890: 
3891: **Pre-trained weights availability** ([source](https://github.com/NVlabs/SegFormer)):
3892: - ImageNet-1K pre-trained encoders for MiT-B0 through MiT-B5
3893: - ADE20K fine-tuned full models on HF: `nvidia/segformer-b0-finetuned-ade-512-512` through `nvidia/segformer-b5-finetuned-ade-640-640`
3894: - Cityscapes fine-tuned models also available
3895: - HuggingFace: `nvidia/segformer-*` model family
3896: 
3897: **Benchmark accuracy** ([source](https://proceedings.neurips.cc/paper/2021/file/64f1f27bf1b4ec22924fd0acb550c235-Paper.pdf)):
3898: 
3899: | Model | Params | ADE20K mIoU | Cityscapes mIoU | FLOPs |
3900: |-------|--------|-------------|-----------------|-------|
3901: | B0 | 3.8M | 37.4% | 76.2% | 8.4G |
3902: | B1 | 13.7M | 42.2% | 78.5% | 15.6G |
3903: | B2 | 24.7M | 46.5% | 81.0% | 64.2G |
3904: | B3 | 44.6M | 49.4% | 82.5% | 96.6G |
3905: | B4 | 61.4M | 50.3% | 82.3% | 95.7G |
3906: | B5 | 81.4M | 51.8% | 84.0% | 183.3G |
3907: 
3908: B0 already beats DeepLabV3+ (MobileNetV2) by 3.4% mIoU at 7.4 FPS faster. ([source](https://arxiv.org/abs/2105.15203))
3909: 
3910: **GPU memory**: B0 fits in **~2GB** at 512×512; B1 in ~4GB; B2+ need 8GB+
3911: 
3912: **Ecosystem**:
3913: - `transformers` library: `SegformerForSemanticSegmentation` + `SegformerImageProcessor`
3914: - `segmentation-models-pytorch` (SMP): SegFormer architecture supported
3915: - MMSegmentation v0.13.0 (official NVlabs repo)
3916: - Keras CV also supports SegFormer
3917: 
3918: **Fine-tuning on custom data** ([official HF cookbook](https://huggingface.co/learn/cookbook/semantic_segmentation_fine_tuning_inference)):
3919: ```python
3920: from transformers import SegformerForSemanticSegmentation, SegformerImageProcessor
3921: model = SegformerForSemanticSegmentation.from_pretrained(
3922:     "nvidia/segformer-b0-finetuned-ade-512-512",
3923:     num_labels=N_CLASSES,
3924:     ignore_mismatched_sizes=True
3925: )
3926: ```
3927: 
3928: **💡 Why it wins for your use case**: The hierarchical Transformer encoder captures both local and global context — crucial when you have few training examples. The MLP decoder is lightweight (fewer trainable params to overfit). HuggingFace Trainer API handles the entire training loop.
3929: 
3930: ---
3931: 
3932: ### 1.2 DeepLabV3+ (CNN-based)
3933: 
3934: | Property | Value |
3935: |----------|-------|
3936: | **Paper** | Encoder-Decoder with Atrous Separable Convolution for Semantic Image Segmentation (Chen et al., ECCV 2018) |
3937: | **Backbones** | ResNet-50 (42M), ResNet-101 (61M), MobileNet-V3-Large (11M) |
3938: | **Architecture** | Atrous Spatial Pyramid Pooling (ASPP) + encoder-decoder with skip connections |

3941: - **MobileNet-V3-Large**: COCO VOC-20 pre-trained (60.3 mIoU, **11.0M params**, 10.45 GFLOPs)

3943: - **ResNet-101**: COCO VOC-20 pre-trained (67.4 mIoU, **61.0M params**, 258.7 GFLOPs)
3944: - All in torchvision → `deeplabv3_resnet50`, `deeplabv3_resnet101`, `deeplabv3_mobilenet_v3_large`

3980: ### 1.3 U-Net (with modern backbones)
3981: 
3982: | Property | Value |
3983: |----------|-------|
3984: | **Paper** | U-Net: Convolutional Networks for Biomedical Image Segmentation (Ronneberger et al., MICCAI 2015) |
3985: | **Modern variants** | U-Net, U-Net++, EfficientUNet++, FPN, Linknet, PSPNet, MAnet — all in SMP |
3986: | **Best backbones for small data** | EfficientNet-b0 (4M), ResNet-18 (11M), MobileNet-V2 (2M) |
3987: 
3988: **Pre-trained weights** ([SMP docs](https://smp.readthedocs.io/en/latest/encoders.html)):
3989: - 500+ encoder backbones, all with ImageNet pre-training
3990: - EfficientNet-b0 through b7 (Imagenet, AdvProp, Noisy-Student)
3991: - ResNet-18 through ResNet-152 (ImageNet, SSL, SWSL)
3992: - Mix Vision Transformer (mit) — same encoder as SegFormer!
3993: - MobileNet-V2/V3 variants
3994: 
3995: **Ecosystem** ([segmentation-models-pytorch](https://github.com/qubvel/segmentation_models.pytorch)):
3996: ```python
3997: import segmentation_models_pytorch as smp
3998: model = smp.Unet(
3999:     encoder_name="efficientnet-b0",      # 4M params
4000:     encoder_weights="imagenet",
4001:     in_channels=3,
4002:     classes=N_CLASSES,
4003: )
4004: ```
4005: 
4006: **GPU memory**: EfficientNet-b0 U-Net: **~1–2GB** at 256×256. Can train on basically any GPU including laptops.
4007: 
4008: **💡 Why for your use case**: U-Net's symmetric encoder-decoder with skip connections is the **most data-efficient architecture** for segmentation. The medical imaging community has extensively validated this on 30–500 image datasets. Combined with EfficientNet-b0 backbone, you get a model that:
4009: - Has the **fewest parameters** of any viable option (encoder 4M + decoder ~4M = ~8M total)
4010: - Converges in fewer epochs due to direct gradient flow through skip connections
4011: - Is extremely robust with aggressive augmentation
4012: 
4013: **⚠️ Limitation**: Lower ceiling on complex scenes vs. Transformers. If your AOI classes benefit from global context (e.g., "sky", "road"), SegFormer will outperform.
4014: 
4015: ---
4016: 
4017: ### 1.4 Mask2Former — Why NOT Recommended Here
4018: 
4019: | Property | Value |
4020: |----------|-------|
4021: | **Paper** | Masked-attention Mask Transformer for Universal Image Segmentation (Cheng et al., CVPR 2022) |
4022: | **Best weights** | `facebook/mask2former-swin-tiny-ade-semantic` (47.4M params) |
4023: | **Benchmark** | 57.7 mIoU on ADE20K — **state of the art** |
4024: | **Architecture** | Masked-attention Transformer decoder + multi-scale deformable attention pixel decoder |
4025: 
4026: **Why not for 40–120 images** ([source](https://debuggercafe.com/fine-tuning-mask2former/)):
4027: - Even the "tiny" variant has 47.4M params with Swin-T backbone — massive overparameterization for tiny data
4028: - The mask classification paradigm (predict N binary masks + class labels) adds unnecessary complexity for simple semantic segmentation
4029: - Official training recipes expect 160K iterations on datasets like ADE20K (20K+ images)
4030: - One published fine-tuning example used 498 training samples and got 22.7% mIoU — still struggled with convergence ([DebuggerCafe fine-tuning tutorial](https://debuggercafe.com/fine-tuning-mask2former/))
4031: 
4032: **When to revisit**: When you have 500+ annotated images and need state-of-the-art results.
4033: 
4034: ---
4035: 
4036: ### 1.5 SAM / SAM 2 — Why NOT Recommended Here
4037: 
4038: | Property | Value |
4039: |----------|-------|
4040: | **Paper** | Segment Anything (Kirillov et al., ICCV 2023); SAM 2 (2024) |
4041: | **Model sizes** | ViT-B (94M), ViT-L (312M), ViT-H (641M); SAM 2: tiny/small/base-plus/large |
4042: | **Design** | Promptable segmentation (points, boxes, masks) — NOT direct semantic segmentation |
4043: | **Fine-tuning** | Requires LoRA, adapters, or full fine-tuning of mask decoder |
4044: 
4045: **Why not for this use case** ([nature article on SAM fine-tuning](https://www.nature.com/articles/s41598-025-97802-w)):
4046: - SAM is designed for **prompt-based** segmentation, not direct pixel classification
4047: - Converting SAM to semantic segmentation requires architectural changes (adding classification heads)
4048: - Even with LoRA (rank=4), the ViT-B image encoder is 94M params — still too large for 40–120 images
4049: - The fixed 1024×1024 input size increases GPU memory 4–8× vs. 512×512 models
4050: - Fine-tuning the mask decoder alone (4.1M params) gives 4–7% Dice drop vs. full fine-tuning on medical benchmarks ([SAM best practices paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2404.09957))
4051: - Parameter-efficient fine-tuning methods (LoRA, adapters) help but still require 200+ images for stable convergence
4052: - GSAM (Generalized SAM) addresses some issues but adds complexity
4053: 
4054: **When to revisit**: For zero-shot or few-shot (1–10 image) scenarios, or when you have 1000+ images and want to use SAM as a backbone with LoRA.
4055: 
4056: ---
4057: 
4058: ## 2. Best Practices for Small-Dataset Fine-Tuning
4059: 
4060: ### 2.1 Data Preparation from CVAT
4061: 
4062: CVAT supports [multiple export formats](https://docs.cvat.ai/docs/dataset_management/formats/_print/). For semantic segmentation:
4063: 
4064: | CVAT Export Format | Best For | Conversion Path |
4065: |-------------------|----------|----------------|
4066: | **Segmentation Mask 1.0** | **Most recommended** — exports PNG masks directly | Directly compatible with all frameworks |
4067: | COCO 1.0 (with masks) | When you need polygon-based annotations | Convert to mask or use COCO dataset class |
4068: | CVAT for images 1.1 | CVAT SDK PyTorch adapter | Use `TaskVisionDataset` directly |
4069: | Datumaro | Advanced pipelines | `datum transform -t polygons_to_masks` then convert |
4070: 
4071: **Recommended pipeline**:
4072: 
4073: 1. In CVAT, **export as "Segmentation Mask 1.0"** format
4074:    - This gives you a ZIP with `img/` (original images) and `mask/` (class-index PNG masks)
4075:    - Mask values: 0 = background, 1 = class1, 2 = class2, ...
4076: 2. The `labelmap.txt` file maps colors → class indices
4077: 
4078: ```python
4079: # Minimal PyTorch Dataset for CVAT Segmentation Mask export
4080: import cv2, torch, glob
4081: from torch.utils.data import Dataset
4082: 
4083: class CVATSegDataset(Dataset):
4084:     def __init__(self, img_dir, mask_dir, transform=None):
4085:         self.imgs = sorted(glob.glob(f"{img_dir}/*"))
4086:         self.masks = sorted(glob.glob(f"{mask_dir}/*"))
4087:         self.transform = transform
4088: 
4089:     def __len__(self):
4090:         return len(self.imgs)
4091: 
4092:     def __getitem__(self, idx):
4093:         image = cv2.imread(self.imgs[idx])
4094:         image = cv2.cvtColor(image, cv2.COLOR_BGR2RGB)
4095:         mask = cv2.imread(self.masks[idx], cv2.IMREAD_GRAYSCALE)
4096:         if self.transform:
4097:             augmented = self.transform(image=image, mask=mask)
4098:             image, mask = augmented["image"], augmented["mask"]
4099:         return torch.tensor(image).permute(2,0,1).float() / 255, \
4100:                torch.tensor(mask).long()
4101: ```
4102: 
4103: **Alternative: CVAT SDK PyTorch adapter** ([CVAT docs](https://docs.cvat.ai/docs/api_sdk/sdk/pytorch-adapter/)):
4104: ```python
4105: from cvat_sdk import Client
4106: from cvat_sdk.pytorch import TaskVisionDataset
4107: client = Client("https://app.cvat.ai")
4108: client.login(("user", "pass"))
4109: dataset = TaskVisionDataset(client, TASK_ID)
4110: ```
4111: This directly reads annotations from CVAT server — no export step needed. Supports transform pipelines.
4112: 
4113: ### 2.2 Data Augmentation (Critical for 40–120 images)
4114: 
4115: With only 40–120 images, **aggressive data augmentation is the single most impactful technique**. Based on the [SegFormer HF fine-tuning cookbook](https://huggingface.co/learn/cookbook/semantic_segmentation_fine_tuning_inference) and [Albumentations semantic segmentation examples](https://albumentations.ai/docs/examples/pytorch-semantic-segmentation/):
4116: 
4117: ```python
4118: import albumentations as A
4119: 
4120: train_transform = A.Compose([
4121:     # 1. Spatial (affects both image and mask)
4122:     A.RandomResizedCrop(height=512, width=512, scale=(0.5, 1.0), p=0.8),
4123:     A.HorizontalFlip(p=0.5),
4124:     A.VerticalFlip(p=0.3),           # AOI often orientation-agnostic
4125:     A.Rotate(limit=45, p=0.7),
4126:     A.ShiftScaleRotate(shift_limit=0.1, scale_limit=0.2, rotate_limit=30, p=0.5),
4127: 
4128:     # 2. Non-rigid (critical for small datasets)
4129:     A.OneOf([
4130:         A.ElasticTransform(alpha=50, sigma=5, p=0.5),
4131:         A.GridDistortion(p=0.5),
4132:         A.OpticalDistortion(p=0.5),
4133:     ], p=0.5),
4134: 
4135:     # 3. Photometric (image only, no effect on mask)
4136:     A.RandomBrightnessContrast(brightness_limit=0.3, contrast_limit=0.3, p=0.8),
4137:     A.HueSaturationValue(hue_shift_limit=10, sat_shift_limit=25, val_shift_limit=20, p=0.5),
4138:     A.GaussNoise(var_limit=(10, 50), p=0.4),
4139:     A.GaussianBlur(blur_limit=(3, 5), p=0.3),
4140:     A.CLAHE(p=0.3),
4141: ])
4142: ```
4143: 
4144: **Key augmentation principles**:
4145: - **RandomResizedCrop** with scale (0.5–1.0) effectively multiplies your dataset by 5–10× in practice
4146: - **Non-rigid transforms** (ElasticTransform) are uniquely valuable for small datasets — they teach deformation invariance without needing more data
4147: - **Photometric transforms** prevent overfitting to lighting/color conditions in your 40 images
4148: - Always use **Albumentations** (not torchvision transforms) for segmentation — it handles mask interpolation correctly
4149: 
4150: ### 2.3 Loss Functions for Small Datasets
4151: 
4152: Based on the [survey of segmentation loss functions](https://ar5iv.labs.arxiv.org/html/2006.14822) and [Unified Focal Loss paper](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC8785124/):
4153: 
4154: | Loss | Best For | Notes |
4155: |------|----------|-------|
4156: | **Dice + CrossEntropy (Combo Loss)** | **🏆 General recommendation** | `α * Dice + (1-α) * CE` — handles class imbalance + smooth gradients |
4157: | **Unified Focal Loss** | Extreme class imbalance | Single γ hyperparameter to tune; best on 2D medical benchmarks |
4158: | **CrossEntropy only** | Balanced classes only | Not recommended for small data (overfits to majority class) |
4159: | **Dice only** | Very small foreground objects | Can have unstable gradients early in training |
4160: | **Focal Loss** | Hard-to-classify boundary pixels | γ=2 is standard; down-weights confident predictions |
4161: 
4162: **Recommended for your use case**: **Combo Loss** (Dice + CrossEntropy)
4163: 
4164: ```python
4165: import torch.nn as nn
4166: import torch.nn.functional as F
4167: 
4168: class ComboLoss(nn.Module):
4169:     def __init__(self, alpha=0.5, smooth=1e-6):
4170:         super().__init__()
4171:         self.alpha = alpha
4172:         self.smooth = smooth
4173: 
4174:     def forward(self, pred, target):
4175:         # CE component
4176:         ce = F.cross_entropy(pred, target)
4177: 
4178:         # Dice component
4179:         pred_softmax = F.softmax(pred, dim=1)
4180:         target_onehot = F.one_hot(target, pred.shape[1]).permute(0,3,1,2).float()
4181: 
4182:         intersection = (pred_softmax * target_onehot).sum(dim=(2,3))
4183:         union = pred_softmax.sum(dim=(2,3)) + target_onehot.sum(dim=(2,3))
4184:         dice = (2. * intersection + self.smooth) / (union + self.smooth)
4185:         dice_loss = 1 - dice.mean()
4186: 
4187:         return self.alpha * dice_loss + (1 - self.alpha) * ce
4188: ```
4189: 
4190: For extreme class imbalance (e.g., 95% background, 5% AOI), use **Unified Focal Loss** from [mlyg/unified-focal-loss](https://github.com/mlyg/unified-focal-loss) — it consistently outperforms other losses on imbalanced medical segmentation benchmarks.
4191: 
4192: ### 2.4 Training Recipe for 40–120 Images
4193: 
4194: Based on published recipes and best practices:
4195: 
4196: ```
4197: 🔄 EPOCHS:              150–300 (more epochs needed with small data)
4198: 📦 BATCH SIZE:          4–16 (as large as GPU allows)
4199: 🚀 LEARNING RATE:       2e-5 to 5e-5 (SegFormer), 1e-4 to 1e-3 (DeepLabV3+), 1e-4 (U-Net)
4200: 📉 SCHEDULER:           Cosine annealing with warmup (50 steps warmup)
4201: 💉 AUGMENTATION:        Aggressive (see above) — on-the-fly, not saved to disk
4202: ❄️ FREEZE STRATEGY:     Freeze encoder for first 10–20 epochs, then unfreeze
4203: ⚖️ LOSS:                Combo Loss (Dice + CE, α=0.5)
4204: 🛑 EARLY STOPPING:      Patience 20–30 epochs on validation mIoU
4205: 🔀 VALIDATION SPLIT:    20% (stratified if multi-class)
4206: 🏋️ MIXED PRECISION:    Use torch.cuda.amp for 2× speed, less memory
4207: ```
4208: 
4209: **Critical small-dataset techniques**:
4210: 
4211: 1. **Freeze encoder pretraining** for first 10–20 epochs while the randomly initialized decoder head stabilizes. This prevents the decoder from destroying the encoder's pre-trained features with random gradients.
4212: 2. **Use smaller input resolution** (e.g., 384×384 instead of 512×512) — you gain 2× more effective batch size and the model learns features at a scale appropriate for your data size.
4213: 3. **Label smoothing** (ε=0.1) reduces overconfidence on tiny datasets.
4214: 4. **Dropout in decoder** (0.1–0.2) provides regularization.
4215: 
4216: ---
4217: 
4218: ## 3. Quantitative Comparison Table
4219: 
4220: | Criterion | SegFormer-B0 | DeepLabV3+ MobileNet-V3 | U-Net EfficientNet-b0 |
4221: |-----------|-------------|------------------------|----------------------|
4222: | **Year** | 2021 | 2018 | 2015 (U-Net core) |
4223: | **Params (total)** | **3.8M** | 11.0M | ~8M (4M enc + ~4M dec) |
4224: | **GPU memory (512²)** | ~2 GB | ~2.5 GB | ~1.5 GB |
4225: | **Train on laptop** | ✅ Yes | ✅ Yes | ✅ Yes (easiest) |
4226: | **Pre-trained weights** | ImageNet + ADE20K/Cityscapes | COCO + ImageNet backbone | ImageNet (all backbones) |
4227: | **Lines to fine-tune** | ~5 (HF transformers) | ~3 (torchvision) | ~3 (SMP) |
4228: | **mIoU on ADE20K** | 37.4% (B0) | 60.3% (COCO-VOC only) | N/A (varies by backbone) |
4229: | **Small-data robustness** | High (Transformer global context) | Medium | **Very High** (skip connections) |
4230: | **Overfitting risk (40 imgs)** | Low–Medium | Medium | **Lowest** |
4231: | **Augmentation compatibility** | Excellent | Good | Excellent |
4232: | **Ecosystem** | HF transformers, SMP, MMSeg | torchvision, SMP, MMSeg | **SMP** (best ecosystem) |
4233: | **Inference speed** | Fast (48 FPS@512) | Very fast (MobileNet) | Fast |
4234: | **Training time (100 epochs)** | ~30 min (T4) | ~20 min (T4) | ~15 min (T4) |
4235: 
4236: ---
4237: 
4238: ## 4. Recommended Pipeline Architecture
4239: 
4240: ### Primary Recommendation: Segmentation Models PyTorch (SMP)
4241: 
4242: SMP is the single best library for your use case because it provides **all three** recommended architectures under one API, with 500+ encoder backbones:
4243: 
4244: ```python
4245: import segmentation_models_pytorch as smp
4246: 
4247: # Option 1: SegFormer via SMP (if you want Transformer)
4248: model = smp.Segformer(
4249:     encoder_name="mit_b0",           # MiT-B0 encoder
4250:     encoder_weights="imagenet",
4251:     classes=N_CLASSES,
4252: )
4253: 
4254: # Option 2: U-Net with EfficientNet (most data-efficient)
4255: model = smp.Unet(
4256:     encoder_name="efficientnet-b0",
4257:     encoder_weights="imagenet",
4258:     classes=N_CLASSES,
4259: )
4260: 
4261: # Option 3: DeepLabV3+ with ResNet-50 (balanced)
4262: model = smp.DeepLabV3Plus(
4263:     encoder_name="resnet50",
4264:     encoder_weights="imagenet",
4265:     classes=N_CLASSES,
4266: )
4267: ```
4268: 
4269: SMP also provides built-in loss functions:
4270: ```python
4271: from segmentation_models_pytorch.losses import DiceLoss, FocalLoss, SoftBCEWithLogitsLoss
4272: 
4273: # Combo loss in one line
4274: loss = DiceLoss(mode='multiclass') + nn.CrossEntropyLoss()
4275: ```
4276: 
4277: **Install**: `pip install segmentation-models-pytorch`
4278: 
4279: ---
4280: 
4281: ## 5. Final Recommendation
4282: 
4283: ### Start with U-Net + EfficientNet-b0 via SMP
4284: 
4285: For the first experimental phase (40–120 images), this combination gives you the **fastest iteration speed** and **lowest risk of overfitting**. Concrete steps:
4286: 
4287: | Step | Action |
4288: |------|--------|
4289: | 1 | Export from CVAT as **Segmentation Mask 1.0** (PNG masks + images) |
4290: | 2 | Split: 80% train / 20% validation |
4291: | 3 | Implement `CVATSegDataset` (see above) with aggressive Albumentations |
4292: | 4 | Use SMP `Unet(encoder_name="efficientnet-b0")` |
4293: | 5 | Loss: `DiceLoss + CrossEntropyLoss` |
4294: | 6 | LR: 1e-4, CosineAnnealing, 200 epochs |
4295: | 7 | Freeze encoder for first 15 epochs |
4296: | 8 | Evaluate with mIoU, save best checkpoint |
4297: 
4298: ### When to upgrade
4299: 
4300: After the initial experiment:
4301: - **If results are promising but you want higher accuracy** → Switch to **SegFormer-B0** (Transformer gives better global context)
4302: - **If you collect 300+ images** → Try **SegFormer-B2** or **DeepLabV3+ ResNet-101**
4303: - **If you get 1000+ images** → Consider **Mask2Former-Swin-Tiny** or **SAM with LoRA**
4304: - **If model is fast enough but class boundaries are fuzzy** → Add boundary-aware loss term to Combo Loss
4305: 
4306: ### Verdict
4307: 
4308: > **For 40–120 images on custom AOI classes, use U-Net with EfficientNet-b0 backbone via segmentation-models-pytorch. Train for 200 epochs with aggressive Albumentations augmentation, Combo Loss (Dice + CE), and cosine annealing. This gives the lowest overfitting risk, fastest iteration, and highest probability of a useful first model. Upgrade to SegFormer-B0 for higher accuracy once the pipeline is validated.**
4309: ```
4310:

4472: 
4473: ## 🔬 模型推荐
4474: 
4475: 基于你的数据情况（39-120张、11类、6000×4000高分辨率、类别不均衡），我推荐三个方案：
4476: 
4477: ---
4478: 
4479: ### 🥇 方案A：U-Net + EfficientNet-b0 (推荐首选)
4480: 
4481: | 指标 | 说明 |
4482: |------|------|
4483: | 参数量 | ~8M (最小的可用方案) |
4484: | GPU 需求 | ~1.5GB @ 512²（笔记本可跑） |
4485: | 预训练权重 | ImageNet |
4486: | 小数据效果 | **最佳** — 跳跃连接结构天然抗过拟合 |
4487: | 库 | `segmentation-models-pytorch`（SMP） |
4488: 
4489: ```python
4490: import segmentation_models_pytorch as smp
4491: model = smp.Unet("efficientnet-b0", encoder_weights="imagenet", classes=11)
4492: ```
4493: 
4494: ✅ 优点：数据效率最高，医学影像界在 50-500 张数据上验证过，最不容易过拟合  
4495: ⚠️ 缺点：复杂场景精度天花板低于 Transformer
4496: 
4497: ---
4498: 
4499: ### 🥈 方案B：SegFormer-B0 (平衡之选)
4500: 
4501: | 指标 | 说明 |
4502: |------|------|
4503: | 参数量 | 3.8M（比 U-Net 还小！） |
4504: | GPU 需求 | ~2GB @ 512² |
4505: | 预训练权重 | ImageNet + ADE20K/Cityscapes |
4506: | 小数据效果 | **良好** — Transformer 全局上下文强 |
4507: | 库 | HuggingFace `transformers` 或 SMP |
4508: 
4509: ```python
4510: from transformers import SegformerForSemanticSegmentation
4511: model = SegformerForSemanticSegmentation.from_pretrained(
4512:     "nvidia/segformer-b0-finetuned-ade-512-512",
4513:     num_labels=11, ignore_mismatched_sizes=True
4514: )
4515: ```
4516: 
4517: ✅ 优点：Transformer 捕捉全局上下文，MLP 解码器轻量不过拟合；HF 官方有完整 fine-tune 教程  
4518: ⚠️ 缺点：学习率敏感，需要 warmup + cosine annealing
4519: 
4520: ---
4521: 
4522: ### 🥉 方案C：DeepLabV3+ MobileNet-V3 (最快迭代)
4523: 
4524: | 指标 | 说明 |
4525: |------|------|
4526: | 参数量 | 11M |
4527: | GPU 需求 | ~2.5GB @ 520² |
4528: | 预训练权重 | COCO + ImageNet |
4529: | 小数据效果 | 中等 |
4530: | 库 | torchvision 原生 |
4531: 
4532: ```python
4533: import torchvision
4534: model = torchvision.models.segmentation.deeplabv3_mobilenet_v3_large(
4535:     num_classes=11
4536: )
4537: ```
4538: 
4539: ✅ 优点：零额外依赖，ASPP 多尺度上下文，迭代最快  
4540: ⚠️ 缺点：CNN 在小数据上不如 U-Net/Transformer 稳健
4541: 
4542: ---
4543: 
4544: ### ❌ 不推荐此阶段：SAM、Mask2Former
4545: 
4546: - **SAM**: 94M+ 参数，设计目标是 prompt-based 分割，不是像素分类，需要大量改造
4547: - **Mask2Former**: 47M 参数（tiny版本），需要 500+ 张数据才能收敛
4548: 
4549: ---
4550: 
4551: ### 🏆 我的推荐：**方案A (U-Net + EfficientNet-b0)**
4552: 
4553: 理由：你的数据量（40张实验阶段）下，**抗过拟合是第一优先级**。U-Net 的跳跃连接结构使信息流直接从编码器到解码器，在小数据上收敛最稳定。等实验跑通后，如果追求更高精度，再升级到 SegFormer-B0。
4554: 
4555: ---

4780: ### 🤖 Assistant
4781: *2026-05-21 23:33:31*
4782: 
4783: *[step-start part]*
4784: 
4785: 💭 **Reasoning:**
4786: 
4787: <details>
4788: <summary>Click to expand reasoning</summary>
4789: 
4790: Now let me present the full pipeline design. With 8-12GB GPU, SegFormer-B1 becomes the best choice:
4791: 
4792: - 13.7M params, ~4GB @ 512²
4793: - 42.2 mIoU on ADE20K
4794: - Transformer global context is helpful for this scene understanding task (urban scenes)
4795: - We can even do larger batch sizes or higher resolution
4796: 
4797: Let me present the design in sections as per the brainstorming checklist. Let me start with the overall architecture and data pipeline.
4798: 
4799: </details>
4800: 
4801: ## 🏗️ Pipeline 设计 v1
4802: 
4803: ### 架构总览
4804: 
4805: ```
4806: CVAT 原始数据                    预处理                     训练                    评估
4807: ┌──────────────┐     ┌─────────────────────┐    ┌─────────────────┐    ┌──────────────┐
4808: │ 南原图/*.JPG │     │ RGB mask → class idx│    │ SegFormer-B1    │    │ mIoU         │
4809: │ (6000×4000)  │ ──→ │ 80/20 train/val     │ ──→│ 512×512 tile    │ ──→│ per-class IoU│
4810: │ 南新/SegClass│     │ Albumentations aug  │    │ Combo Loss      │    │ confusion    │
4811: │ *.png (RGB)  │     │ save as .pt tiles   │    │ 200 epochs      │    │ matrix       │
4812: └──────────────┘     └─────────────────────┘    └─────────────────┘    └──────────────┘
4813: ```
4814: 
4815: ### 1. 模型选型：SegFormer-B1
4816: 
4817: 8-12GB 显存下，**SegFormer-B1** 是最优解：
4818: 
4819: | 为什么选 B1 | 
4820: |-------------|
4821: | 13.7M 参数，~4GB 显存，留有充足余量做 batch=16 或 640² 输入 |
4822: | Transformer 层级编码器捕捉全局上下文 → "天空""建筑界面""绿化景观"受益 |
4823: | ADE20K/Cityscapes 预训练权重直接可用，语义域与城市场景高度匹配 |
4824: | HuggingFace 有官方 fine-tune cookbook，代码量极小 |
4825: 
4826: 备选：如果想更快迭代或担心过拟合，随时可降级到 SegFormer-B0（3.8M）。
4827: 
4828: ### 2. 数据管线设计
4829: 
4830: **核心问题**：6000×4000 → 太大，必须切 tile。同时 mask 是 RGB 彩色编码，需要转 class index。
4831: 
4832: ```
4833: 项目结构：
4834: E:\CVAT\
4835: ├── 南原图/           ← 原始 JPG（不动）
4836: ├── 南新/             ← 原始标注（不动）
4837: ├── data/             ← 新建：预处理后数据
4838: │   ├── train/
4839: │   │   ├── images/   ← 512×512 tile (JPG/PNG)
4840: │   │   └── masks/    ← 512×512 grayscale class index (PNG)
4841: │   └── val/
4842: │       ├── images/
4843: │       └── masks/
4844: ├── src/
4845: │   ├── preprocess.py     ← 预处理脚本
4846: │   ├── dataset.py        ← PyTorch Dataset
4847: │   ├── train.py          ← 训练主脚本
4848: │   └── config.py         ← 配置集中管理
4849: ├── checkpoints/          ← 模型保存
4850: └── logs/                 ← TensorBoard 日志
4851: ```
4852: 
4853: **预处理步骤** (`preprocess.py`)：
4854: 
4855: ```
4856: 1. 读取 labelmap.txt → 建立 RGB→class_id 映射表
4857: 2. 遍历每对 (JPG, SegmentationClass.png)
4858: 3. 将 RGB mask 转换为 single-channel class index
4859: 4. 切分为 512×512 重叠 tile (stride=384, overlap=128)
4860: 5. 80/20 train/val 按原图维度 split（确保同一原图的 tile 不跨 split）
4861: 6. 保存为 (image_tile.png, mask_tile.png)
4862: ```
4863: 
4864: **Class index 转换核心逻辑**：
4865: 
4866: ```python
4867: # labelmap.txt → RGB→ID 映射表
4868: color_to_id = {
4869:     (0,0,0): 0, (12,54,138): 1, (131,214,41): 2,
4870:     (180,40,5): 3, (103,22,84): 4, (97,196,248): 5,
4871:     (233,161,3): 6, (60,5,5): 7, (12,170,34): 8, (78,78,78): 9,
4872: }
4873: 
4874: def rgb_to_class_id(rgb_mask: np.ndarray) -> np.ndarray:
4875:     """6000×4000×3 RGB → 6000×4000 uint8 class IDs"""
4876:     class_mask = np.zeros(rgb_mask.shape[:2], dtype=np.uint8)
4877:     for rgb, cls_id in color_to_id.items():
4878:         class_mask[np.all(rgb_mask == rgb, axis=2)] = cls_id
4879:     return class_mask
4880: ```
4881: 
4882: ### 3. 训练配置
4883: 
4884: ```python
4885: # config.py
4886: CONFIG = {
4887:     # 模型
4888:     "model_name": "nvidia/segformer-b1-finetuned-ade-512-512",
4889:     "num_classes": 11,
4890:     "image_size": 512,
4891: 
4892:     # 数据
4893:     "batch_size": 8,           # 8-12GB 建议 8 (安全)
4894:     "num_workers": 4,
4895:     "train_split": 0.8,
4896: 
4897:     # 优化
4898:     "learning_rate": 3e-5,     # SegFormer 官方推荐
4899:     "weight_decay": 0.01,
4900:     "epochs": 200,
4901:     "warmup_steps": 50,
4902:     "lr_scheduler": "cosine",
4903: 
4904:     # 正则化
4905:     "dropout": 0.1,            # decoder dropout
4906:     "label_smoothing": 0.0,    # 先不加，过拟合再加
4907: 
4908:     # 损失
4909:     "loss": "combo",           # Dice + CrossEntropy (α=0.5)
4910: 
4911:     # 保存
4912:     "save_top_k": 3,
4913:     "early_stop_patience": 30,
4914: }
4915: ```
4916: 
4917: ### 4. 数据增强策略 (Albumentations)
4918: 
4919: 40 张图的小数据集，**增强是最重要的环节**：
4920: 
4921: ```python
4922: train_aug = A.Compose([
4923:     # 空间变换（图和 mask 同步）
4924:     A.RandomResizedCrop(512, 512, scale=(0.5, 1.0), p=1.0),
4925:     A.HorizontalFlip(p=0.5),
4926:     A.Rotate(limit=30, p=0.7),
4927:     A.ShiftScaleRotate(shift_limit=0.1, scale_limit=0.2, rotate_limit=15, p=0.5),
4928: 
4929:     # 非刚性形变（小数据集关键）
4930:     A.OneOf([
4931:         A.ElasticTransform(alpha=50, sigma=5),
4932:         A.GridDistortion(),
4933:     ], p=0.3),
4934: 
4935:     # 光度变换（仅图像，不动 mask）
4936:     A.RandomBrightnessContrast(brightness_limit=0.2, contrast_limit=0.2, p=0.7),
4937:     A.HueSaturationValue(hue_shift_limit=10, sat_shift_limit=20, val_shift_limit=15, p=0.4),
4938:     A.GaussNoise(var_limit=(10, 50), p=0.3),
4939: ])
4940: 
4941: val_aug = A.Compose([
4942:     A.Resize(512, 512),  # 验证集不做随机增强
4943: ])
4944: ```
4945: 
4946: ### 5. 训练策略
4947: 
4948: ```
4949: Phase 1 (epochs 1-15):  冻结 encoder，仅训练 decoder head
4950:                         LR=1e-4, warmup=50 steps
4951: Phase 2 (epochs 16-200): 解冻全部，LR=3e-5
4952:                         cosine annealing to 1e-6
4953: ```
4954: 
4955: **为什么分阶段**：随机初始化的 decoder 在初期产生大梯度会破坏 encoder 预训练特征。先让 decoder 收敛再联合训练，能保留更多预训练知识。
4956: 
4957: ### 6. 评估方案
4958: 
4959: - **主指标**: mIoU（所有类平均）、per-class IoU
4960: - **辅助**: Pixel Accuracy、Dice Score
4961: - **可视化**: 每 20 epoch 随机采样验证集图片，保存预测 mask vs 真值 mask 对比图
4962: - **关注重点**: 稀有类（文化装饰 1.5%、车 1.1%）的 IoU 是否崩塌
4963: 
4964: ---
4965: 
4966: 这个设计是否符合你的预期？有哪些部分需要调整？确认后我写完整 spec 文档并规划实现步骤。

5372: 
5373: **为什么选它（你 8-12GB 显卡的最佳选择）**：
5374: 
5375: - **13.7M 参数**，显存占用 ~4GB，batch=8 无压力
5376: - **Transformer 架构**，捕捉全局上下文（"天空""建筑界面""绿化景观"这种大区域类受益最大）

5379:

5381:

5383: 
5384: ### 🔧 Pipeline 四步走
5385: 
5386: ```
5387: 原始数据 → 预处理 → 训练 → 评估
5388: ```
5389: 
5390: **① 预处理** — 最关键的一步
5391: - RGB 彩色 mask → 单通道 class index（0-9）
5392: - 6000×4000 大图 → 512×512 tile（重叠切分，一张原图 ~50 个 tile）
5393: - 80/20 按原图维度划分训练集/验证集（防止 tile 泄露）
5394: 
5395: **② 数据增强** — 40 张图就靠它
5396: - 随机裁剪缩放、翻转、旋转、弹性形变、亮度对比度、噪声
5397: - 用 Albumentations 库，训练时在线增强，不存盘
5398: 
5399: **③ 训练**
5400: - 分两阶段：先冻结 backbone 训 15 epoch decoder → 再全解冻训 185 epoch
5401: - 学习率 3e-5，余弦退火，warmup 50 步
5402: - 损失函数 = 0.5 × Dice + 0.5 × CrossEntropy（兼顾类别不均衡）
5403: 
5404: **④ 评估**
5405: - mIoU（主指标）+ 每类 IoU
5406: - 每 20 epoch 可视化 4 张验证集预测结果
5407:

5525: Now I can give a comprehensive answer about model options. The user wants to know what other models they can choose besides SegFormer-B1. Let me organize this clearly.
5526: 
5527: Key considerations for this task:
5528: - ~40 images (120 eventually)
5529: - 8-12GB GPU
5530: - 11 classes with class imbalance

5532: - 6000×4000 high-res images
5533: 
5534: Let me categorize models by their architecture family and give practical advice for each.
5535: 
5536: </details>
5537: 
5538: ## 可选模型全览（按架构分家族）
5539: 
5540: ### ① Transformer 家族（编码器-解码器，全局依赖）
5541: 
5542: | 模型 | 参数量 | 显存~ | 小数据 | 预训练 | 推荐度 |
5543: |------|--------|-------|--------|--------|--------|
5544: | **SegFormer-B0** | 3.8M | 2GB | ⭐⭐⭐ | ADE/City | 🔥🔥🔥 |
5545: | **SegFormer-B1** | 13.7M | 4GB | ⭐⭐⭐ | ADE/City | 🔥🔥🔥 |
5546: | **SegFormer-B2** | 24.7M | 6GB | ⭐⭐ | ADE/City | 🔥🔥 |
5547: | **SETR-PUP** | 96M | ~8GB | ⭐ | ADE/City | ❌ |
5548: 
5549: - **优点**: 全局感受野不用像 CNN 叠层数，小物体和多尺度好，HuggingFace 开箱即用
5550: - **缺点**: 位置编码是插值得到的，极端分辨率需要多切 tile
5551: 
5552: ---
5553: 
5554: ### ② CNN Encoder-Decoder（金字塔，多尺度）
5555: 
5556: | 模型 | 骨架 | 参数量 | 显存~ | 小数据 | 特点 |
5557: |------|------|--------|-------|--------|------|
5558: | **DeepLabV3+ + MobileNetV3-Large** | MobileNetV3 | 11M | 2.5GB | ⭐⭐ | torchvision 原生，ASPP 多尺度 |
5559: | **DeepLabV3+ + ResNet50** | ResNet50 | 59M | ~5GB | ⭐ | 精度高于 MobileNet 版 |
5560: | **DeepLabV3+ + ResNet101** | ResNet101 | 75M | ~7GB | ⭐ | 更强但 40 张跑不动 |
5561: | **PSPNet + ResNet50** | ResNet50 | 49M | ~4.5GB | ⭐ | PPM 金字塔池化 |
5562: | **FCN + ResNet50** | ResNet50 | 32M | ~3GB | ⭐⭐ | 最经典 baseline |
5563: 
5564: - **DeepLabV3+**: 你是 AOI 场景，空洞卷积（ASPP）本身就是为多尺度城区设计的——和你的任务天然契合
5565: - **PSPNet**: 和 DeepLab 同级别，但社区生态不如 torchvision 的 DeepLab 方便
5566: 
5567: ---
5568: 
5569: ### ③ U-Net 家族（跳跃连接，抗过拟合）
5570: 
5571: | 模型 | 骨架 | 参数量 | 显存~ | 小数据 | 特点 |
5572: |------|------|--------|-------|--------|------|
5573: | **U-Net + EfficientNet-b0** | Eff-b0 | 8M | 1.5GB | ⭐⭐⭐ | 最小，最快 |
5574: | **U-Net + EfficientNet-b3** | Eff-b3 | 22M | ~4GB | ⭐⭐⭐ | 精度/速度最佳折中 |
5575: | **U-Net + ResNet34** | ResNet34 | 24M | ~3GB | ⭐⭐⭐ | 纯熟稳定 |
5576: | **U-Net + ResNet50** | ResNet50 | 44M | ~4.5GB | ⭐⭐ | 精度略高，需更多数据 |
5577: | **FPN + EfficientNet-b3** | Eff-b3 | 21M | ~3.5GB | ⭐⭐⭐ | 特征金字塔，多尺度好 |
5578: 
5579: > 全部通过 `segmentation-models-pytorch`（SMP）库一个接口搞定，三行代码换模型。**这是小数据微调的银弹**
5580: 
5581: - **优点**: 跳跃连接在 40 张图上是最强抗过拟合武器，Encoder 特征直接传给 Decoder——比 Transformer 对数据量要求友好太多
5582: - **缺点**: 纯 CNN 感受野受限于 kernel size，超长范围依赖弱于 Transformer
5583: 
5584: ---
5585: 
5586: ### ④ ConvNeXt / 现代 CNN（SOTA 精度，新骨架）
5587: 
5588: | 模型 | 骨架 | 参数量 | 显存~ | 小数据 | 特点 |
5589: |------|------|--------|-------|--------|------|
5590: | **U-Net + ConvNeXt-T** | ConvNeXt-T | 40M | ~5GB | ⭐⭐ | 2020s 最强 CNN 骨架 |
5591: | **U-Net + ConvNeXt-S** | ConvNeXt-S | 64M | ~7GB | ⭐ | 可能撑不住 |
5592: 
5593: ConvNeXt 吸收了 Transformer 的设计思想用到 CNN 上（GELU、LayerNorm、大 kernel 7×7），精度接近 Swin Transformer。但 40 张图喂不饱。
5594: 
5595: ---
5596: 
5597: ### ⑤ 轻量级实时模型（推理快，精度中等）
5598: 
5599: | 模型 | 参数量 | 显存~ | 推理 | 小数据 |
5600: |------|--------|-------|------|--------|
5601: | **PIDNet-S** | 7.6M | 2GB | 极快 | ⭐⭐ |
5602: | **STDC1** | 7.3M | 2GB | 快 | ⭐⭐ |
5603: | **PP-LiteSeg-T** | 6.0M | 1.5GB | 极快 | ⭐ |
5604: 
5605: 这些是工业部署用的。训练代码得手写，社区生态不如 SMP/HF。不推荐你现在用。
5606: 
5607: ---
5608: 
5609: ## 🧭 我应该怎么选？
5610: 
5611: 按你的阶段（40 张实验 → 120 张上产）：
5612: 
5613: | 你的优先考虑 | 第一选择 | 第二选择 |
5614: |-------------|---------|---------|
5615: | **最容易上手、代码量最小** | SegFormer-B1（HF） | U-Net+Eff-b3（SMP） |
5616: | **40 张过拟合最小** | U-Net+ResNet34（SMP） | U-Net+Eff-b3（SMP） |
5617: | **AOI 多尺度场景最佳** | SegFormer-B1 | DeepLabV3+MobileNet |
5618: | **想快速对比实验** | SMP 全家桶（U-Net/DeepLabV3+/FPN） | SegFormer |
5619: | **纯精度，不 care 显存** | SegFormer-B2 | DeepLabV3+ResNet50 |
5620: | **数据未来会到 500+ 张** | ConvNeXt-T U-Net | SegFormer-B2 |
5621: 
5622: ---
5623: 
5624: ## 🎯 我的建议：A/B 双跑方案
5625: 
5626: 实验阶段与其只跑一个，不如**两个差异化的模型各跑一遍**，用数据说话：
5627: 
5628: - **方案 A**: SegFormer-B1 — 代表 Transformer 路线，HF 生态
5629: - **方案 B**: U-Net + EfficientNet-b3 — 代表 CNN + 跳跃连接路线，SMP 生态
5630: 
5631: 两个都用 SMP 和 HF 各一套代码就能跑。训练完对比 mIoU：哪个好就用哪个上 120 张。
5632: 
5633: ---
5634: 
5635: 你觉得哪个方向更合心意？确认后我出实现计划。
5636: 
5637: *[step-finish part]*
5638: 
5639: ---

6332: 53: 
6333: 54: # Brainstorming Ideas Into Designs
6334: 55: 
6335: 56: Help turn ideas into fully formed designs and specs through natural collaborative dialogue.
6336: 57: 
6337: 58: Start by understanding the current project context, then ask questions one at a time to refine the idea. Once you understand what you're building, present the design and get user approval.
6338: 59: 
6339: 60: <HARD-GATE>
6340: 61: Do NOT invoke any implementation skill, write any code, scaffold any project, or take any implementation action until you have presented a design and the user has approved it. This applies to EVERY project regardless of perceived simplicity.
6341: 62: </HARD-GATE>
6342: 63: 
6343: 64: ## Anti-Pattern: "This Is Too Simple To Need A Design"
6344: 65: 
6345: 66: Every project goes through this process. A todo list, a single-function utility, a config change — all of them. "Simple" projects are where unexamined assumptions cause the most wasted work. The design can be short (a few sentences for truly simple projects), but you MUST present it and get approval.
6346: 67: 
6347: 68: ## Checklist
6348: 69: 
6349: 70: You MUST create a task for each of these items and complete them in order:
6350: 71: 
6351: 72: 1. **Explore project context** — check files, docs, recent commits
6352: 73: 2. **Offer visual companion** (if topic will involve visual questions) — this is its own message, not combined with a clarifying question. See the Visual Companion section below.
6353: 74: 3. **Ask clarifying questions** — one at a time, understand purpose/constraints/success criteria
6354: 75: 4. **Propose 2-3 approaches** — with trade-offs and your recommendation
6355: 76: 5. **Present design** — in sections scaled to their complexity, get user approval after each section
6356: 77: 6. **Write design doc** — save to `docs/superpowers/specs/YYYY-MM-DD-<topic>-design.md` and commit
6357: 78: 7. **Spec self-review** — quick inline check for placeholders, contradictions, ambiguity, scope (see below)
6358: 79: 8. **User reviews written spec** — ask user to review the spec file before proceeding
6359: 80: 9. **Transition to implementation** — invoke writing-plans skill to create implementation plan
6360: 81: 
6361: 82: ## Process Flow
6362: 83:

67: ## 2. Model Selection: SegFormer-B1
68: 
69: ### 2.1 Why SegFormer-B1
70: 
71: | Factor | Decision |
72: |--------|----------|
73: | GPU (8-12GB) | B1 uses ~4GB @ 512², leaves room for batch=8–16 |
74: | Pre-training | ADE20K/Cityscapes — scene parsing domain matches urban AOI |
75: | Architecture | Hierarchical Transformer (MiT) captures global context critical for sky/building/vegetation classes |
76: | Overfitting risk | MLP decoder is lightweight (fewer params to overfit on 40 imgs) |
77: | Ecosystem | HuggingFace `transformers` with official fine-tune cookbook |
78: 
79: ### 2.2 Alternatives
80: 
81: | Scenario | Switch to |
82: |----------|-----------|
83: | Overfitting observed | SegFormer-B0 (3.8M, even lighter decoder) |
84: | Need faster iteration | DeepLabV3+ MobileNet-V3 (11M, torchvision native) |
85: | 120+ images later | SegFormer-B2 (24.7M, higher accuracy ceiling) |
86: 
87: ### 2.3 What We're NOT Using
88: 
89: - **SAM**: Prompt-based design, 94M params requiring LoRA adapters. Wrong paradigm for semantic segmentation.
90: - **Mask2Former**: 47M params (tiny). Mask classification + masked attention too complex for 40-image dataset.
91: - **U-Net**: Viable, but Transformer global context edges it out for urban scene parsing.
92:

95: ## 3. Pipeline Architecture
96: 
97: ```
98: RAW DATA              PREPROCESSING              TRAINING                EVALUATION
99: ─────────             ─────────────              ────────                ──────────
100: 南原图/*.JPG    ──┐                    ┌── Dataset class      ┌── mIoU
101:                   ├── preprocess.py ──┤  (Albumentations) ──┤── per-class IoU
102: 南新/SegClass    ──┘                    └── DataLoader ───────┘── confusion matrix
103:   /*.png (RGB)         │                       │                    │
104:                        ▼                       ▼                    ▼
105:                   RGB→class idx          SegFormer-B1         TensorBoard
106:                   80/20 split            HF Trainer           sample pred viz
107:                   512² tiles             Combo Loss            best checkpoint
108:                   saved to data/          200 epochs            early stopping
109: ```

118: ├── 南新/                      # Original annotations (read-only)
119: ├── data/                      # Preprocessed training data (generated)

142: | `dataset.py` | data/{train,val}/ dirs | (image_tensor, mask_tensor) batches | albumentations, torch |
143: | `train.py` | config.py, dataset.py | checkpoints/, logs/ | transformers, torch |
144: | `evaluate.py` | checkpoint, val split | mIoU, per-class IoU, viz | torch, sklearn |
145:

148: ## 5. Training Configuration
149: 
150: ### 5.1 Hyperparameters
151: 
152: ```python
153: CONFIG = {
154:     "model_name": "nvidia/segformer-b1-finetuned-ade-512-512",
155:     "num_classes": 11,
156:     "image_size": 512,
157: 
158:     "batch_size": 8,
159:     "num_workers": 4,
160:     "train_split": 0.8,
161: 
162:     "learning_rate": 3e-5,
163:     "weight_decay": 0.01,
164:     "epochs": 200,
165:     "warmup_steps": 50,
166:     "lr_scheduler": "cosine",
167: 
168:     "dropout": 0.1,
169:     "label_smoothing": 0.0,
170: 
171:     "loss_alpha": 0.5,       # Dice weight in combo loss
172:     "save_top_k": 3,
173:     "early_stop_patience": 30,
174: }
175: ```
176: 
177: ### 5.2 Two-Phase Training
178: 
179: ```
180: Phase 1 (epochs 1–15):
181:   - Freeze encoder (MiT-B1 backbone)
182:   - Train decoder head only
183:   - LR: 1e-4 (higher since decoder starts random)
184:   - Purpose: stabilize decoder before joint training
185: 
186: Phase 2 (epochs 16–200):
187:   - Unfreeze all parameters
188:   - LR: 3e-5 → cosine anneal to 1e-6
189:   - Purpose: fine-tune full model
190: ```
191: 
192: ### 5.3 Loss Function: Combo Loss
193: 
194: ```python
195: loss = 0.5 * DiceLoss(mode='multiclass') + 0.5 * CrossEntropyLoss()
196: ```
197: 
198: Dice handles class imbalance; CE provides smooth gradients. No class weighting needed with this combination.
199: 
200: ### 5.4 Data Augmentation (Albumentations)
201: 
202: Critical for 40-image dataset. Applied on-the-fly per epoch:
203: 
204: | Transform | Target | Probability | Rationale |
205: |-----------|--------|-------------|-----------|
206: | RandomResizedCrop(512, scale=0.5-1.0) | Image+Mask | 1.0 | Effective 5-10× dataset expansion |
207: | HorizontalFlip | Image+Mask | 0.5 | Scene symmetry |
208: | Rotate(±30°) | Image+Mask | 0.7 | Orientation invariance |
209: | ElasticTransform | Image+Mask | 0.3 | Deformation robustness |
210: | BrightnessContrast | Image only | 0.7 | Lighting variation |
211: | HueSaturationValue | Image only | 0.4 | Color variation |
212: | GaussNoise | Image only | 0.3 | Sensor noise robustness |
213: 
214: Validation: only `Resize(512, 512)` — no augmentation.
215: 
216: ### 5.5 Split Strategy
217: 
218: - 80/20 split at **original image level** (not tile level)
219: - Ensures tiles from the same image don't leak across train/val
220: - With 39 images: 31 train, 8 val
221: - After tiling (512², stride=384, overlap=128): ~2000 train tiles, ~500 val tiles (estimated)
222: 
223: ---
224: 
225: ## 6. Evaluation & Success Criteria
226: 
227: ### 6.1 Metrics
228: 
229: - **Primary**: mIoU (mean Intersection over Union across all 11 classes)
230: - **Secondary**: Per-class IoU, Pixel Accuracy, Dice Score
231: - **Diagnostic**: Confusion matrix, class frequency vs prediction frequency
232: 
233: ### 6.2 Target Thresholds (Experimental Phase)
234: 
235: | Metric | Minimum Acceptable | Good | Excellent |
236: |--------|-------------------|------|-----------|
237: | mIoU | > 40% | > 55% | > 65% |
238: | Rare class IoU (crowd, decor, vehicles) | > 15% | > 30% | > 45% |
239: | Dominant class IoU (sky, commercial, building) | > 50% | > 65% | > 75% |
240: 
241: ### 6.3 Visual Verification
242: 
243: Every 20 epochs: save 4 random validation samples with side-by-side (original → ground truth → prediction). This catches issues metrics miss (boundary quality, small object handling).
244: 
245: ### 6.4 Known Risks
246: 
247: 1. **Rare class collapse**: Classes 0, 7, 9 may get 0 IoU. Mitigated by Combo Loss. If still failing, add per-class Dice weighting.
248: 2. **Overfitting**: 39 images is small. Mitigated by aggressive augmentation + early stopping. Monitor train/val gap.
249: 3. **Tile boundary artifacts**: Overlap=128 stride=384 ensures smooth predictions. Post-inference stitching needed for full-image eval.
250: 
251: ---
252: 
253: ## 7. Implementation Plan (Outline)
254: 
255: | Phase | Steps | Est. Time |
256: |-------|-------|-----------|
257: | **0. Environment** | Create conda env, install torch + transformers + albumentations + SMP | 30 min |
258: | **1. Preprocessing** | Implement `preprocess.py` (RGB→idx, tile, split), run on 39 images | 1 hr |
259: | **2. Dataset** | Implement `dataset.py` with Albumentations pipeline | 30 min |
260: | **3. Training** | Implement `train.py`, run 200 epochs | 3-6 hrs (GPU) |
261: | **4. Evaluation** | Implement `evaluate.py`, compute metrics, generate viz | 30 min |
262: | **5. Iterate** | Tune hyperparams based on results, re-train if needed | Variable |
263: 
264: ---
